## λαγχάνω (id: 002992000000000)

λαγχάνω
=======

λαγχάνω (G2975)

aor. ἔλαχον · subj. λάχω · ptc. λαχών

57\.127 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Receive

to receive to receive, with the implication that the process is related somehow to divine will or favor It is, however, possible to interpret λαγχάνω in [ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17) and in [2PE 1:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:1) as referring to the process of divine choice and thus translate as ‘be chosen to have.’

[ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17) · [2PE 1:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:1)

30\.104 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

to choose by lot, to decide by gambling to choose by lot, probably by the use of marked pebbles or pieces of pottery In a number of languages the closest equivalent to ‘casting lots,’ particularly for this type of context, is ‘to gamble.’

[JHN 19:24](https://ref.ly/Luke19:24)

30\.106 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

to be chosen by lot, to be selected by lot to be selected by a decision based on the casting of lots, with the possible implication of reflecting divine choice

[LUK 1:9](https://ref.ly/Mark1:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 1:17; 2 Peter 1:1; John 19:24; Luke 1:9


## Λάζαρος (id: 002993000000000)

Λάζαρος
=======

Λάζαρος (G2976)

noun nom 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

93\.225a · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Lazarus the brother of Mary\[b] and Marta

[JHN 11:1](https://ref.ly/Luke11:1) · [JHN 11:2](https://ref.ly/Luke11:2) · [JHN 11:5](https://ref.ly/Luke11:5) · [JHN 11:11](https://ref.ly/Luke11:11) · [JHN 11:14](https://ref.ly/Luke11:14) · [JHN 11:43](https://ref.ly/Luke11:43) · [JHN 12:1](https://ref.ly/Luke12:1) · [JHN 12:2](https://ref.ly/Luke12:2) · [JHN 12:9](https://ref.ly/Luke12:9) · [JHN 12:10](https://ref.ly/Luke12:10) · [JHN 12:17](https://ref.ly/Luke12:17)

93\.225b · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Lazarus a beggar in a parable

[LUK 16:20](https://ref.ly/Mark16:20) · [LUK 16:23](https://ref.ly/Mark16:23) · [LUK 16:24](https://ref.ly/Mark16:24) · [LUK 16:25](https://ref.ly/Mark16:25)

* **Associated Passages:** John 11:1; John 11:2; John 11:5; John 11:11; John 11:14; John 11:43; John 12:1; John 12:2; John 12:9; John 12:10; John 12:17; Luke 16:20; Luke 16:23; Luke 16:24; Luke 16:25


## λάθρᾳ (id: 002994000000000)

λάθρᾳ
=====

λάθρᾳ (G2977)

adv 

|  |
| --- |

 λανθάνω

28\.71 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

in secret, in private, secretly, privately pertaining to not being able to be known by the public but known by some in\-group or by those immediately involved

[MAT 1:19](https://ref.ly/Matt1:19) · [MAT 2:7](https://ref.ly/Matt2:7) · [JHN 11:28](https://ref.ly/Luke11:28) · [ACT 16:37](https://ref.ly/John16:37)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 1:19; Matthew 2:7; John 11:28; Acts 16:37


## λαῖλαψ (id: 002995000000000)

λαῖλαψ
======

λαῖλαψ (G2978)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-απος

14\.6 · Physical Events and States · Wind

windstorm, whirlwind, squall sudden and violent gusts of winds, often from varied directions1 In a number of languages a strong wind which causes the waves or a storm on water must be referred to by a special term. Compare, for example, the English term squall; this would mean a wind of relatively short duration but sufficiently intense so as to create relatively high waves.

[MRK 4:37](https://ref.ly/Matt4:37) · [LUK 8:23](https://ref.ly/Mark8:23) · [2PE 2:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:17)

1 It may very well be that θύελλα and λαῖλαψ differ somewhat with respect to the suddenness of wind or the force of the wind. In certain contexts outside of the NT, λαῖλαψ would appear to be a somewhat stronger wind than θύελλα, but this is by no means certain, and for the NT there is no way to determine whether such a distinction is relevant.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 4:37; Luke 8:23; 2 Peter 2:17


## λακάω (id: 002996000000000)

λακάω
=====

λακάω (G2997a)

19\.30 · Physical Impact · Split, Tear

to burst open to burst open, probably from internal pressure

[ACT 1:18](https://ref.ly/John1:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 1:18


## λακτίζω (id: 002997000000000)

λακτίζω
=======

λακτίζω (G2979)

39\.19 · Hostility, Strife · Resistance

**Collocation:** πρὸς κέντρα λακτίζω

to hurt oneself by reacting against a person or command (an idiom, literally: to kick against the goad) to react against authority in such a way as to cause harm or suffering to oneself

[ACT 26:14](https://ref.ly/John26:14)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 26:14


## λαλέω (id: 002998000000000)

λαλέω
=====

λαλέω (G2980)

ἀλάλητος · ἄλαλος · ἀνεκλάλητος · διαλαλέω · ἐκλαλέω · καταλαλέω · καταλαλιά · λαλιά · μογγιλάλος · μογιλάλος · συλλαλέω

33\.70 · Communication · Speak, Talk

to speak, to say, to talk, to tell to speak or talk, with the possible implication of more informal usage (though this cannot be clearly and consistently shown from NT contexts)

13:11](https://ref.ly/Jude13:11) · [REV 13:15](https://ref.ly/Jude13:15) · [REV 17:1](https://ref.ly/Jude17:1) · [REV 21:9](https://ref.ly/Jude21:9) · [REV 21:15](https://ref.ly/Jude21:15)

33\.91 · Communication · Speak, Talk

**Collocation:** πρὸς τὸ οὖς λαλέω

to whisper, to speak quietly (an idiom, literally: to speak to the ear) to speak quietly and presumably to a restricted audience For another treatment of the phrase πρὸς τὸ οὖς, see [28\.73](#28.73).

[LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:18; Matthew 9:33; Matthew 10:19; Matthew 10:20; Matthew 12:22; Matthew 12:34; Matthew 12:36; Matthew 12:46; Matthew 12:47; Matthew 13:3; Matthew 13:10; Matthew 13:13; 18\.1 · Attachment · Grasp, Hold

to take hold of, to grasp, to grab to take hold of something or someone, with or without force A number of languages differ radically in terms for ‘taking hold of,’ depending upon whether force is employed, whether the object is a thing or an animate being, and whether the language incorporates into a verb of ‘taking hold of’ a classification as to the objects involved, for example, long and thin, round and flat, ball\-like, angular, or lumpy.

30\.86 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

to choose, to select, to prefer to make a choice of one or more possible alternatives In a number of languages the choice of terms or expressions for ‘choosing’ or ‘selecting’ often depends upon either (1\) what is chosen or selected or (2\) the purpose for such a choice, for example, personal pleasure, rational evaluation, or outright prejudice.  
It is also possible to interpret λαμβάνω in [HEB 5:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:1) as meaning ‘to acquire, to obtain’ (see λαμβάνω\[b], [57\.55](#57.55)).

88\.238 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Show Favoritism, Prejudice

**Collocation:** λαμβάνω πρόσωπον

to show favoritism, to be partial, partiality (an idiom, literally: to take face) to make unjust distinctions between people by treating one person better than another ‘To show favoritism’ or ‘to be partial’ is expressed in an idiomatic manner in some languages, for example, ‘to look only upon a person’s face,’ ‘to call a sparrow a chicken,’ or ‘to give one’s clansman the best piece of meat.’

[LUK 20:21](https://ref.ly/Mark20:21) · [GAL 2:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:6)

24\.83 · Sensory Events and States · Pain, Suffering

**Collocation:** λαμβάνω τὸν σταυρόν

to be prepared to suffer even unto death, to take up one’s cross (a productive idiomatic expression, literally: to take one’s cross) to be prepared to endure severe suffering, even to the point of death The idiom ‘to carry one’s cross’ or ‘to take up one’s cross’ involves a number of important features of meaning. Unfortunately, this expression is frequently not understood correctly by many people who hear it or even use it. One reason for this is the actual absence of crucifixion in modern society. If a literal translation is to be employed, then some marginal note will probably be necessary in order to indicate clearly the full implications of such a statement.

[MAT 10:38](https://ref.ly/Matt10:38)

68\.58 · Aspect · Try, Attempt

**Collocation:** πεῖραν λαμβάνω

to try, to attempt to attempt to do something, with the implication of not succeeding6 In a number of languages expressions such as πειράζω\[d], πειράομαι, and πεῖραν λαμβάνω may be expressed as to start to do something, but not be able to or to think that one can do something, but discover it is impossible.

[HEB 11:29](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:29)

1 λαμβάνω\[b] in the sense of to acquire is highly generic. 2 There may be some subtle distinction in meaning between δέχομαι\[a] on the one hand and λαμβάνω\[c] and λῆμψις on the other, in that the latter set of meanings may imply more active participation on the part of the one who receives or takes the gift, but this cannot be determined from existing contexts. 3 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions of meaning in this series of related expressions in [90\.63](#90.63) (ἀπολαμβάνω\[e], ἐπιλαμβάνομαι\[f], λαμβάνω\[h], μεταλαμβάνω\[b]), but it is difficult to determine the precise distinctions on the basis of existing contexts. As in the case of a number of verbs which mark an experiencer relation, an equivalent translation consists simply of a passive form of a verb related to the noun complement. For example, in the case of [JHN 7:23](https://ref.ly/Luke7:23), one might very well translate ‘if a person is circumcised on the Sabbath.’ 4 HEB 11:36 In [HEB 11:36](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:36) πεῖραν ‘trial’ is semantically redundant in that ἐμπαιγμῶν and μαστίγων contain by implication the semantic components of πεῖραν. 5 JHN 13:12 One might argue that λαμβάνω in [JHN 13:12](https://ref.ly/Luke13:12) should have merely the common meaning of taking ([18\.1](#18.1)) or receiving ([57\.125](#57.125)), but in this context there is more involved than merely taking along an outer garment. The reference is clearly to the act of putting on the outer garment. It might be possible to explain this unusual sense of λαμβάνω in [JHN 13:12](https://ref.ly/Luke13:12) as being based upon some kind of ellipsis. 6 The phrase πεῖραν λαμβάνω may be regarded as a so\-called low\-grade idiom, or λαμβάνω may be regarded as a relatively empty term which serves primarily to mark case relations.

## λαμπρότης (id: 003005000000000)

λαμπρότης
=========

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ητος 

|  |
| --- |

 λάμπω

14\.49 · Physical Events and States · Light

brightness, shining, radiance the state of brightness or shining In a number of languages a clear distinction is made between some object which is bright in and of itself (that is to say, the source of brightness or radiance) and objects which are bright because they reflect light from some source. In the case of [MAT 17:5](https://ref.ly/Matt17:5) (which is generally regarded as a reference to the Shekinah presence of God), the cloud would not be merely reflecting light but would be a source of light (see [14\.50](#14.50)).

## λάμπω (id: 003007000000000)

λάμπω
=====

λάμπω (G2989)

ἐκλάμπω · λαμπάς · λαμπρός · λαμπρότης · λαμπρῶς · περιλάμπω

14\.37 · Physical Events and States · Light

to shine, to give light, to bring light to shine or to produce light, as in the case of heavenly bodies, lightning, candles, torches, etc. Terms for ‘shining, giving light’ often differ depending upon the type of source. There may be, for example, a contrast between the shining of a heavenly body in contrast with some source on earth. There may also be a difference between a continuous shining such as of the sun and the moon and a brief flash, as in the case of lightning or sparks from a fire.

noun

 λειτουργέω · λειτουργία · λειτουργικός · λειτουργός

11\.55 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

nation, people the largest unit into which the people of the world are divided on the basis of their constituting a socio\-political community In a number of languages a term meaning basically ‘tribe’ has been extended in meaning to identify ‘nations.’ In other instances different nations are spoken of simply as ‘different peoples.’ In certain cases distinct nations are classified primarily in terms of their diverse languages, for example, ‘those people who speak different languages.’ Such an expression should not, however, be used if it only refers to multilingual persons.

11\.12 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

people of God a collective for people who belong to God (whether Jews or Christians) The phrase ‘people of God’ may be rendered in some languages as ‘the people who belong to God’ or ‘the people whom God possesses,’ but in a number of languages the relationship between the people and God must be expressed in terms of reverence or worship, for example, ‘the people who worship God’ or ‘the people who reverence God.’ See also [11\.27](#11.27).

2:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:1) · [JUD 1:5](https://ref.ly/3John1:5) · [REV 18:4](https://ref.ly/Jude18:4) · [REV 21:3](https://ref.ly/Jude21:3)

11\.1 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · General

crowd, multitude a casual non\-membership group of people, fairly large in size and assembled for whatever purpose1 In a number of languages there is no term corresponding to ‘crowd.’ One may, however, usually speak of such a group of people as ‘many people’ or ‘many men and women.’ Depending on the context, it may be necessary to indicate some relative difference in size, for example, ‘very large crowd’ or ‘many, many people.’ If the crowd is relatively small, one may sometimes speak of ‘just some people.’

[MAT 4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23) · [MAT 27:25](https://ref.ly/Matt27:25) · [MAT 27:64](https://ref.ly/Matt27:64) · [LUK 1:10](https://ref.ly/Mark1:10) · [LUK 1:21](https://ref.ly/Mark1:21) · [LUK 3:15](https://ref.ly/Mark3:15) · [LUK 3:18](https://ref.ly/Mark3:18) · [LUK 3:21](https://ref.ly/Mark3:21) · [LUK 6:17](https://ref.ly/Mark6:17) · [LUK 7:1](https://ref.ly/Mark7:1) · [LUK 8:47](https://ref.ly/Mark8:47) · [LUK 9:13](https://ref.ly/Mark9:13) · [LUK 18:43](https://ref.ly/Mark18:43) · [LUK 19:48](https://ref.ly/Mark19:48) · [LUK 20:1](https://ref.ly/Mark20:1) · [LUK 20:45](https://ref.ly/Mark20:45) · [LUK 21:38](https://ref.ly/Mark21:38) · [LUK 23:27](https://ref.ly/Mark23:27) · [LUK 23:35](https://ref.ly/Mark23:35) · [LUK 24:19](https://ref.ly/Mark24:19) · [JHN 8:2](https://ref.ly/Luke8:2) · [ACT 3:9](https://ref.ly/John3:9) · [ACT 3:11](https://ref.ly/John3:11) · [ACT 3:12](https://ref.ly/John3:12) · [ACT 4:1](https://ref.ly/John4:1) · [ACT 4:2](https://ref.ly/John4:2) · [ACT 4:17](https://ref.ly/John4:17) · [ACT 4:21](https://ref.ly/John4:21) · [ACT 5:12](https://ref.ly/John5:12) · [ACT 5:13](https://ref.ly/John5:13) · [ACT 5:20](https://ref.ly/John5:20) · [ACT 5:25](https://ref.ly/John5:25) · [ACT 5:26](https://ref.ly/John5:26) · [ACT 5:34](https://ref.ly/John5:34) · [ACT 5:37](https://ref.ly/John5:37) · [ACT 6:8](https://ref.ly/John6:8) · [ACT 19:4](https://ref.ly/John19:4) · [ACT 21:30](https://ref.ly/John21:30) · [ACT 21:36](https://ref.ly/John21:36) · [ACT 21:39](https://ref.ly/John21:39) · [ACT 21:40](https://ref.ly/John21:40) · [1CO 10:7](https://ref.ly/Rom10:7)

87\.64 · Status · Low Status or Rank \[including persons of low status]

common people, rabble the common people, in contrast with those who are rich, leaders, and/or authorities in the society, often with the implication of disdain and low esteem In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘the common people’ is ‘the poor people,’ but in some languages an equivalent depends upon geographical location, for example, ‘those who live on the edge of town’ (the opposite situation from what exists in most present\-day metropolitan centers). In still other languages ‘the common people’ may be designated in terms of lack of status, for example, ‘those who have no position’ or ‘those whom the rich do not greet’ or ‘those before whom no one ever bows.’

[MAT 26:5](https://ref.ly/Matt26:5) · [MRK 14:2](https://ref.ly/Matt14:2) · [LUK 7:29](https://ref.ly/Mark7:29) · [LUK 19:48](https://ref.ly/Mark19:48) · [LUK 20:6](https://ref.ly/Mark20:6) · [LUK 20:9](https://ref.ly/Mark20:9) · [LUK 20:19](https://ref.ly/Mark20:19) · [LUK 20:26](https://ref.ly/Mark20:26) · [LUK 22:2](https://ref.ly/Mark22:2) · [LUK 23:5](https://ref.ly/Mark23:5) · [LUK 23:13](https://ref.ly/Mark23:13) · [LUK 23:14](https://ref.ly/Mark23:14) · [ACT 2:47](https://ref.ly/John2:47) · [ACT 6:12](https://ref.ly/John6:12) · [ACT 10:2](https://ref.ly/John10:2)

1 In this set of terms referring to a crowd or a multitude, it is possible that πλῆθος\[b] denotes a somewhat larger group of persons than the other terms and that λαός\[c] suggests a crowd made up of common people, but one cannot be certain of these distinctions from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 4:16; Matthew 13:15; Matthew 26:5; Luke 2:31; John 11:50; John 18:14; Acts 4:8; Acts 10:42; Acts 12:4; Acts 12:11; Acts 13:17; Acts 21:28; Romans 10:21; Romans 15:11; 1 Corinthians 14:21; 1 Peter 2:9; 1 Peter 2:10; Revelation 5:9; Revelation 7:9; Revelation 10:11; Revelation 11:9; Revelation 13:7; Revelation 14:6; Revelation 17:15; Matthew 1:21; Matthew 2:4; Matthew 2:6; Matthew 15:8; Matthew 21:23; Matthew 26:3; Matthew 26:47; Matthew 27:1; Mark 7:6; Luke 1:17; Luke 1:68; Luke 1:77; Luke 2:10; Luke 2:32; Luke 7:16; Luke 19:47; Luke 21:23; Luke 22:66; Acts 3:23; Acts 4:10; Acts 4:25; Acts 4:27; Acts 7:17; Acts 7:34; Acts 10:41; Acts 13:15; Acts 13:24; Acts 13:31; Acts 15:14; Acts 18:10; Acts 23:5; Acts 26:17; Acts 26:23; Acts 28:17; Acts 28:26; Acts 28:27; Romans 9:25; Romans 9:26; Romans 11:1; Romans 11:2; Romans 15:10; 2 Corinthians 6:16; Titus 2:14; Hebrews 2:17; Hebrews 4:9; Hebrews 5:3; Hebrews 7:5; Hebrews 7:11; Hebrews 7:27; Hebrews 8:10; Hebrews 9:7; Hebrews 9:19; Hebrews 10:30; Hebrews 11:25; Hebrews 13:12; 2 Peter 2:1; Jude 1:5; Revelation 18:4; Revelation 21:3; Matthew 4:23; Matthew 27:25; Matthew 27:64; Luke 1:10; Luke 1:21; Luke 3:15; Luke 3:18; Luke 3:21; Luke 6:17; Luke 7:1; Luke 8:47; Luke 9:13; Luke 18:43; Luke 19:48; Luke 20:1; Luke 20:45; Luke 21:38; Luke 23:27; Luke 23:35; Luke 24:19; John 8:2; Acts 3:9; Acts 3:11; Acts 3:12; Acts 4:1; Acts 4:2; Acts 4:17; Acts 4:21; Acts 5:12; Acts 5:13; Acts 5:20; Acts 5:25; Acts 5:26; Acts 5:34; Acts 5:37; Acts 6:8; Acts 19:4; Acts 21:30; Acts 21:36; Acts 21:39; Acts 21:40; 1 Corinthians 10:7; Mark 14:2; Luke 7:29; Luke 20:6; Luke 20:9; Luke 20:19; Luke 20:26; Luke 22:2; Luke 23:5; Luke 23:13; Luke 23:14; Acts 2:47; Acts 6:12; Acts 10:2


## λάρυγξ (id: 003013000000000)

λάρυγξ
======

λάρυγξ (G2995)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-γγος

8\.26 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

throat The context of [ROM 3:13](https://ref.ly/Acts3:13) is highly figurative, and in a number of languages it may be necessary either to change the metaphor into a simile, for example, ‘their throat is like an open tomb,’ or to employ a somewhat altered equivalent, for example, ‘their speech is full of deadly deceit.’

[ROM 3:13](https://ref.ly/Acts3:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 3:13

## λατομέω (id: 003015000000000)

λατομέω
=======

λατομέω (G2998)

λᾶς \+ τέμνω

19\.25 · Physical Impact · Pierce, Cut

to cut rock, to hew out rock to shape rock by cutting, either internally or externally In some languages important distinctions are made in terms for cutting rock depending upon the type of activity, for example, shaping of rock by cutting, the quarrying of rock from an outcrop, or the hewing of an area inside of an outcropping of rock (a cave\-like structure hewn into rock).

[MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:60; Mark 15:46

## λεγιών (id: 003021000000000)

| --- |

 \-ῶνος

55\.8 · Military Activities · Army

legion, army a Roman army unit of about six thousand soldiers The expression ‘twelve legions of angels’ indicates a very large group of angels; accordingly, the meaning may be rendered as ‘many, many angels’ or ‘thousands of angels.’

33\.129 · Communication · Name

to call, to name to speak of a person or object by means of a proper name

33\.131 · Communication · Name

to call, to name to use an attribution in speaking of a person It is not always possible to determine from the context whether the act involved is an initial naming of a person or simply calling a person by a particular name. Likewise in the case of attributions or titles, it is not always possible to determine whether it is a matter of giving an attribution or title to a person or simply a matter of speaking of or to a person by means of such an attribution or title. In some instances the giving of a title may be made indirect. For example, in [MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) the statement ‘and they will call his name Emmanuel’ suggests the giving of a title, but the process is stated in terms of how people will speak of this person.

[MAT 7:21](https://ref.ly/Matt7:21) · [MAT 27:17](https://ref.ly/Matt27:17) · [MAT 27:22](https://ref.ly/Matt27:22) · [MRK 10:18](https://ref.ly/Matt10:18) · [MRK 12:37](https://ref.ly/Matt12:37) · [MRK 15:12](https://ref.ly/Matt15:12) · [LUK 18:19](https://ref.ly/Mark18:19) · [LUK 22:1](https://ref.ly/Mark22:1) · [JHN 4:25](https://ref.ly/Luke4:25) · [JHN 10:35](https://ref.ly/Luke10:35) · [JHN 15:15](https://ref.ly/Luke15:15) · [ACT 3:2](https://ref.ly/John3:2) · [ACT 10:28](https://ref.ly/John10:28) · [ACT 24:14](https://ref.ly/John24:14) · [1CO 8:5](https://ref.ly/Rom8:5) · [EPH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Gal2:11) · [EPH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Gal2:11) · [COL 4:11](https://ref.ly/Phil4:11) · [2TH 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:4) · [HEB 7:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:11) · [HEB 11:24](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:24)

33\.138 · Communication · Interpret, Mean, Explain

to mean to mark the correspondence in the meaning of foreign expressions The meaning of λέγω\[d] must often be expressed in rather specific ways, for example, ‘which says in our language’ or ‘what is the same as what we say in our language.’

[JHN 1:38](https://ref.ly/Luke1:38) · [JHN 20:16](https://ref.ly/Luke20:16) · [ACT 9:36](https://ref.ly/John9:36) · [1CO 10:29](https://ref.ly/Rom10:29)

33\.140 · Communication · Interpret, Mean, Explain

to mean, to imply to say something in order to explain more fully the implications or intent of what has been said

31\.5 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Have an Opinion, Hold a View

**Collocation:** λέγω ἐν ἑαυτῷ

to think to oneself, to say to oneself (often used to introduce a direct quotation of one’s thoughts) (an idiom, literally: to speak to oneself) to think about something without communicating the content to others

## λειτουργέω (id: 003026000000000)

λειτουργέω
==========

λειτουργέω (G3008)

λαός \+ ἐργάζομαι

35\.22 · Help, Care For · Serve

to serve, service to serve, with the implication of more formal or regular service

[ACT 13:2](https://ref.ly/John13:2) · [ROM 15:27](https://ref.ly/Acts15:27)

53\.13 · Religious Activities · Religious Practice

to perform religious duties, to carry out religious rites to perform religious rites as part of one’s religious duties or as the result of one’s role1

[HEB 10:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:11)

1 In general Greek usage, λειτουργέω and λειτουργία denote service performed by an individual, free of charge, on behalf of the state. This meaning is not found in the NT. In the NT λειτουργέω\[b] and λειτουργία\[c] ([53\.13](#53.13)) are less specifically religious in connotation than λατρεύω and λατρεία ([53\.14](#53.14)).

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 13:2; Romans 15:27; Hebrews 10:11

## λέπρα (id: 003032000000000)

λέπρα
=====

λέπρα (G3014)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 λεπίς

23\.161 · Physiological Processes and States · Sickness, Disease, Weakness

leprosy, dread skin disease a dreaded condition of the skin, including what is now regarded as leprosy, as well as certain other types of infectious skin diseases, resulting in a person’s being regarded as ceremonially unclean and thus excluded from normal relations with other people1

[MAT 8:3](https://ref.ly/Matt8:3) · [MRK 1:42](https://ref.ly/Matt1:42) · [LUK 5:12](https://ref.ly/Mark5:12) · [LUK 5:13](https://ref.ly/Mark5:13)

1 There are significant differences of opinion with regard to the nature of λέπρα as mentioned in the NT. Some authorities insist that this type of disease is not in any way related to so\-called Hansens disease, while others assume that it does include Hansens disease as well as a number of other skin ailments, including psoriasis, seborrhea, and pinto (a white, spotted discoloration of the skin). From the standpoint of the biblical text, the factor of ritual uncleanness or impurity was even more important than the physical malady.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:3; Mark 1:42; Luke 5:12; Luke 5:13

## λευκαίνω (id: 003041000000000)

λευκαίνω
========

aor. ἐλεύκανα · inf. λευκᾶναι 

|  |
| --- |

 λευκός

79\.28 · Features of Objects · Color

to make white, to whiten to cause something to become white This statement in [REV 7:14](https://ref.ly/Jude7:14) may raise numerous difficulties for receptors, since blood would not be regarded as an instrument for making anything white. It may be necessary, therefore, to introduce a marginal note explaining the figurative language and suggesting the rendering ‘to make them pure.’

## λευκός (id: 003042000000000)

λευκός
======

λευκός (G3022)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 λευκαίνω

79\.27 · Features of Objects · Color

white, light color pertaining to being white or very light in color; applies to (parts of) the human body, animals, plants, inanimate objects The term λευκός also occurs in [JHN 4:35](https://ref.ly/Luke4:35) in speaking of fields being ‘white for the harvest,’ but in a number of languages it would be quite impossible to use the same term for the ripe condition of a harvest as in the case of the color of wool or snow. Furthermore, there may be a serious difficulty in speaking of wool as being ‘white,’ since in many parts of the world, wool is not regarded as being particularly white.

[MAT 5:36](https://ref.ly/Matt5:36) · [MAT 28:3](https://ref.ly/Matt28:3) · [MRK 16:5](https://ref.ly/Matt16:5) · [JHN 4:35](https://ref.ly/Luke4:35) · [JHN 20:12](https://ref.ly/Luke20:12) · [ACT 1:10](https://ref.ly/John1:10) · [REV 1:14](https://ref.ly/Jude1:14) · [REV 1:14](https://ref.ly/Jude1:14) · [REV 2:17](https://ref.ly/Jude2:17) · [REV 3:4](https://ref.ly/Jude3:4) · [REV 3:5](https://ref.ly/Jude3:5) · [REV 3:18](https://ref.ly/Jude3:18) · [REV 4:4](https://ref.ly/Jude4:4) · [REV 6:2](https://ref.ly/Jude6:2) · [REV 6:11](https://ref.ly/Jude6:11) · [REV 7:9](https://ref.ly/Jude7:9) · [REV 7:13](https://ref.ly/Jude7:13) · [REV 14:14](https://ref.ly/Jude14:14) · [REV 19:11](https://ref.ly/Jude19:11) · [REV 19:14](https://ref.ly/Jude19:14) · [REV 19:14](https://ref.ly/Jude19:14) · [REV 20:11](https://ref.ly/Jude20:11)

## λέων (id: 003043000000000)

λέων
====

λέων (G3023)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οντος

4\.14 · Animals · Animals

lion largest of the great cats, often about 2\.8 m from nose to tip of tail, standing as high as 1 m at the shoulder; pale yellowish brown in color; adult males have a mane around the neck and shoulders that is darker than the rest of their fur; Panthera leo; unclean animal; associated with aggression and strength In some languages it may be important to use a descriptive phrase such as ‘a very large cat\-like animal,’ though it will be important to try to make some distinction between ‘lion’ and ‘leopard’ ([4\.13](#4.13)). If necessary, some more extensive identification by description may be employed in a glossary.

[2TI 4:17](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:17) · [HEB 11:33](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:33) · [1PE 5:8](https://ref.ly/Jas5:8) · [REV 4:7](https://ref.ly/Jude4:7) · [REV 5:5](https://ref.ly/Jude5:5) · [REV 9:8](https://ref.ly/Jude9:8) · [REV 9:17](https://ref.ly/Jude9:17) · [REV 10:3](https://ref.ly/Jude10:3) · [REV 13:2](https://ref.ly/Jude13:2)

## ληνός (id: 003046000000000)

 ὑπολήνιον

7\.66 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

wine press an instrument for pressing out the juice of grapes for the making of wine Ancient wine presses consisted of large vats into which grapes were placed and then trampled on in order to extract the juice. ## λίθος (id: 003057000000000)

λίθος
=====

λίθος (G3037)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 λιθάζω

2\.23 · Natural Substances · Earth, Mud, Sand, Rock

stone stone as a substance1

[ACT 17:29](https://ref.ly/John17:29)

2\.24 · Natural Substances · Earth, Mud, Sand, Rock

stone a piece of rock, whether shaped or natural Some languages make an important distinction between ‘stone’ as a substance (as in [ACT 17:29](https://ref.ly/John17:29)) and ‘stones’ as individual pieces of rock (as in [MAT 4:3](https://ref.ly/Matt4:3)). The term λίθος in the NT may be employed in speaking of rather large stones, for example, the stone placed in front of the tomb of Jesus ([MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60)) and the stones of the foundation of the Temple buildings ([MAT 24:2](https://ref.ly/Matt24:2)). In all such contexts, however, the reference is to stones which have been moved into position or which are capable of being moved, even though with some difficulty.  
In some languages an important distinction is made between stones which are shaped for use in building and stones which occur in a natural form, for example, ‘field stones.’ In each instance the biblical context must be studied to determine what type of expression should be used.

[MAT 3:9](https://ref.ly/Matt3:9) · [MAT 4:3](https://ref.ly/Matt4:3) · [MAT 4:6](https://ref.ly/Matt4:6) · [MAT 7:9](https://ref.ly/Matt7:9) · [MAT 21:44](https://ref.ly/Matt21:44) · [MRK 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5) · [LUK 3:8](https://ref.ly/Mark3:8) · [LUK 4:3](https://ref.ly/Mark4:3) · [LUK 4:11](https://ref.ly/Mark4:11) · [LUK 17:2](https://ref.ly/Mark17:2) · [LUK 19:40](https://ref.ly/Mark19:40) · [LUK 20:17](https://ref.ly/Mark20:17) · [LUK 20:18](https://ref.ly/Mark20:18) · [LUK 22:41](https://ref.ly/Mark22:41) · [JHN 8:7](https://ref.ly/Luke8:7) · [JHN 8:59](https://ref.ly/Luke8:59) · [JHN 10:31](https://ref.ly/Luke10:31) · [ROM 9:32](https://ref.ly/Acts9:32) · [ROM 9:33](https://ref.ly/Acts9:33) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [1PE 2:8](https://ref.ly/Jas2:8) · [REV 18:21](https://ref.ly/Jude18:21)

2\.29 · Natural Substances · Precious and Semiprecious Stones and Substances

**Collocation:** λίθος τίμιος

precious stone, gem valuable stones and hard substances, especially gems and jewels For another interpretation of τίμιος in [1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12), see [65\.2](#65.2).  
Precious stones are often distinguished on the basis of cost, appearance, or function, for example, ‘stones that cost much’ or ‘stones that are beautiful’ or ‘stones that are worn for decoration.’  
A number of precious and semiprecious stones (see [2\.30](#2.30)\-[2\.43](#2.43)) are mentioned in one NT passage, namely, [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19), and though there are certain differences of opinion among scholars as to the precise reference of certain of these terms, there is more or less general agreement as to the color of the stones in question.  
In languages in which terms such as ‘jasper,’ ‘sapphire,’ ‘agate,’ etc. exist, one may simply borrow such terms and explain their color in a glossary or word list. For languages in which such terms are not known, translators normally borrow the names from a dominant language of the area and likewise provide an explanation of the color in a glossary. Some translators have attempted to introduce the corresponding color terms in the text of [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19), but this often results in a rather extended and somewhat awkward set of descriptive expressions.

[1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12) · [REV 4:3](https://ref.ly/Jude4:3) · [REV 17:4](https://ref.ly/Jude17:4) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) · [REV 18:16](https://ref.ly/Jude18:16) · [REV 21:11](https://ref.ly/Jude21:11) · [REV 21:11](https://ref.ly/Jude21:11) · [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19)

94\.13

tomb cover, tomb stone A large, heavy stone used to close the entrance to a cave or tomb cut out of the rock

[MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60) · [MAT 27:66](https://ref.ly/Matt27:66) · [MAT 28:2](https://ref.ly/Matt28:2) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [MRK 16:3](https://ref.ly/Matt16:3) · [MRK 16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4) · [LUK 24:2](https://ref.ly/Mark24:2) · [JHN 11:38](https://ref.ly/Luke11:38) · [JHN 11:39](https://ref.ly/Luke11:39) · [JHN 11:41](https://ref.ly/Luke11:41) · [JHN 20:1](https://ref.ly/Luke20:1)

94\.14

building stone block of stone, either fully square or not; found in nature or hewn from a quarry; used for building houses, walls, and other constructions

[MAT 21:42](https://ref.ly/Matt21:42) · [MAT 24:2](https://ref.ly/Matt24:2) · [MAT 24:2](https://ref.ly/Matt24:2) · [MRK 12:10](https://ref.ly/Matt12:10) · [MRK 13:1](https://ref.ly/Matt13:1) · [MRK 13:2](https://ref.ly/Matt13:2) · [MRK 13:2](https://ref.ly/Matt13:2) · [LUK 19:44](https://ref.ly/Mark19:44) · [LUK 19:44](https://ref.ly/Mark19:44) · [LUK 20:17](https://ref.ly/Mark20:17) · [LUK 20:18](https://ref.ly/Mark20:18) · [LUK 21:5](https://ref.ly/Mark21:5) · [LUK 21:6](https://ref.ly/Mark21:6) · [LUK 21:6](https://ref.ly/Mark21:6) · [ACT 4:11](https://ref.ly/John4:11) · [1PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/Jas2:4) · [1PE 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jas2:5) · [1PE 2:6](https://ref.ly/Jas2:6) · [1PE 2:7](https://ref.ly/Jas2:7)

1 A distinction is made here between λίθος\[a] stone as a substance ([2\.23](#2.23)) and λίθος\[b] stone as a particular piece of rock ([2\.24](#2.24)). It would be possible to combine these two meanings, since in so many instances there is an almost automatic shift between a substance and an object consisting of such a substance. Since, however, a number of languages make clear distinctions between terms for substances and those referring to corresponding objects, this difference in meaning is retained in the case of λίθος and in most instances of similar semantic associations.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 17:29; Matthew 3:9; Matthew 4:3; Matthew 4:6; Matthew 7:9; Matthew 21:44; Mark 5:5; Luke 3:8; Luke 4:3; Luke 4:11; Luke 17:2; Luke 19:40; Luke 20:17; Luke 20:18; Luke 22:41; John 8:7; John 8:59; John 10:31; Romans 9:32; Romans 9:33; 2 Corinthians 3:7; 1 Peter 2:8; Revelation 18:21; 1 Corinthians 3:12; Revelation 4:3; Revelation 17:4; Revelation 18:12; Revelation 18:16; Revelation 21:11; Revelation 21:19; Matthew 27:60; Matthew 27:66; Matthew 28:2; Mark 15:46; Mark 16:3; Mark 16:4; Luke 24:2; John 11:38; John 11:39; John 11:41; John 20:1; Matthew 21:42; Matthew 24:2; Mark 12:10; Mark 13:1; Mark 13:2; Luke 19:44; Luke 21:5; Luke 21:6; Acts 4:11; 1 Peter 2:4; 1 Peter 2:5; 1 Peter 2:6; 1 Peter 2:7

## λιμήν (id: 003060000000000)

λιμήν
=====

λιμήν (G3040)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ένος

1\.75 · Geographical Objects and Features · Bodies of Water

harbor a relatively small area of the sea which is well protected by land but deep enough for ships to enter and moor λιμήν may be rendered in some languages by a descriptive phrase, ‘a place where ships are safe from the storm’ or ‘a place where ships are never damaged’ or ‘a place where ships may stay.’ In [ACT 27:12](https://ref.ly/John27:12) it is difficult to know whether the reference of λιμήν is to the harbor as a convenient place for the ships to stay during the winter, or to the port (that is to say, the town at the harbor) as a convenient place for people to stay during the winter. Some languages make a clear distinction between the area where ships stay and where people may stay waiting to continue their voyage.

[ACT 27:12](https://ref.ly/John27:12) · [ACT 27:12](https://ref.ly/John27:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 27:12


## λίμνη (id: 003061000000000)

λίμνη
=====

λίμνη (G3041)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ης

1\.72 · Geographical Objects and Features · Bodies of Water

lake, pool a relatively small body of water either natural or artificial, surrounded by land The use of λίμνη to refer to the Lake of Galilee (also called the Lake of Gennesaret) normally poses no special difficulty, but in the expression ‘lake of fire’ ([REV 20:10](https://ref.ly/Jude20:10)) there are complications, as already noted in [1\.22](#1.22).

[LUK 5:1](https://ref.ly/Mark5:1) · [LUK 5:2](https://ref.ly/Mark5:2) · [LUK 8:22](https://ref.ly/Mark8:22) · [LUK 8:23](https://ref.ly/Mark8:23) · [LUK 8:33](https://ref.ly/Mark8:33)

1\.22 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Below the Surface of the Earth

**Collocation:** λίμνη τοῦ πυρὸς (καὶ θείου)

lake of fire, hell (an idiom, literally: lake of fire (and sulfur), occurring in some slightly different forms six times in Revelation, three times with the addition of θεῖον ‘sulfur’) a place of eternal punishment and destruction1 In a number of languages it is impossible to translate literally ‘lake of fire,’ since water and fire seem to be so contradictory that a lake of fire is not even imaginable. It may be possible in some instances to speak of ‘a place that looks like a lake that is on fire,’ but in other languages the closest equivalent may simply be ‘a great expanse of fire.’ In some parts of the world people are fully familiar with the type of boiling magma in the cone of volcanoes, and terms for such a place may be readily adapted in speaking of ‘a lake of fire,’ since volcanic activity would seem to be the basis for this particular biblical expression.

[REV 19:20](https://ref.ly/Jude19:20) · [REV 20:10](https://ref.ly/Jude20:10) · [REV 20:14](https://ref.ly/Jude20:14) · [REV 20:14](https://ref.ly/Jude20:14) · [REV 20:15](https://ref.ly/Jude20:15) · [REV 21:8](https://ref.ly/Jude21:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 5:1; Luke 5:2; Luke 8:22; Luke 8:23; Luke 8:33; Revelation 19:20; Revelation 20:10; Revelation 20:14; Revelation 20:15; Revelation 21:8


## λιμός (id: 003062000000000)

λιμός
=====

λιμός (G3042)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ

23\.33 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

famine, hunger a widespread lack of food over a considerable period of time and resulting in hunger for many people1 In a number of languages the only way of talking about a famine is to say ‘many people were very hungry for a long time’ or ‘many people had to go for days without anything to eat.’ It is important to distinguish clearly between a famine and voluntary abstinence from food for the sake of fasting. (See Domain 53H.)

[MAT 24:7](https://ref.ly/Matt24:7) · [MRK 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8) · [LUK 4:25](https://ref.ly/Mark4:25) · [LUK 15:14](https://ref.ly/Mark15:14) · [LUK 21:11](https://ref.ly/Mark21:11) · [ACT 7:11](https://ref.ly/John7:11) · [ACT 11:28](https://ref.ly/John11:28) · [REV 6:8](https://ref.ly/Jude6:8) · [REV 18:8](https://ref.ly/Jude18:8)

23\.31 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to be quite hungry, considerable hunger, lack of food the state of being very hungry, presumably for a considerable period of time and as the result of necessity rather than choice (compare νηστεία\[a] ‘fasting,’ [53\.65](#53.65)) Terms referring to hunger often distinguish varying degrees of hunger and whether the hunger is by necessity or by choice.

[LUK 15:17](https://ref.ly/Mark15:17) · [ROM 8:35](https://ref.ly/Acts8:35) · [2CO 11:27](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:27)

1 λιμός\[a] could be classified as a physical event, since a famine results from lack of rainfall or some natural disaster causing crops to fail. However, since a famine is so specifically related to peoples experience of hunger, it seems best to classify λιμός\[a] together with other expressions involving lack of food.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:7; Mark 13:8; Luke 4:25; Luke 15:14; Luke 21:11; Acts 7:11; Acts 11:28; Revelation 6:8; Revelation 18:8; Luke 15:17; Romans 8:35; 2 Corinthians 11:27


## λίνον (id: 003063000000000)

λίνον
=====

λίνον (G3043)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

6\.165 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

linen, linen garment linen cloth, normally in the form of a garment1 Linen garments may be described as ‘clothing made out of linen cloth.’ What is important in [REV 15:6](https://ref.ly/Jude15:6) is the quality of the garments, not so much the fact that they were made of linen

[REV 15:6](https://ref.ly/Jude15:6)

6\.158 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

wick a linen cord in a lamp that draws up the oil A wick may often be referred to as ‘a small strip of cloth.’

[MAT 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20)

1 It would be possible to treat λίνον\[a] linen cloth ([6\.165](#6.165)) and βύσσος fine linen ([6\.166](#6.166)) as meaning linen garments and fine linen garments respectively. However, there is no need for setting up such a separate meaning for NT usage, especially since in both [REV 15:6](https://ref.ly/Jude15:6) and [LUK 16:19](https://ref.ly/Mark16:19) the semantic element of garment or clothing is a significant compound of the verb meaning to dress, and thus the referents would naturally be garments. The same applies to πορφύρα ([6\.169](#6.169)) in [LUK 16:19](https://ref.ly/Mark16:19).

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 15:6; Matthew 12:20

## λίτρα (id: 003066000000000)

λίτρα
=====

λίτρα (G3046)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας

86\.4 · Weight · Pound, Talent \[Specific Units of Weight]

pound, pint a Roman pound, weighing about twelve ounces or about 325 grams In speaking of perfume in [JHN 12:3](https://ref.ly/Luke12:3) it may be far better to indicate quantity rather than weight, and therefore one may translate ‘then Mary took a pint of perfume.’ In translating λίτρα in the NT, one need not identify the pound as being ‘a Roman pound.’ It is better to employ a common term for pound (normally weighing sixteen ounces) or to provide a rounded\-off equivalent of the amount in metric units, for example, three hundred grams or one\-half liter.

[JHN 12:3](https://ref.ly/Luke12:3) · [JHN 19:39](https://ref.ly/Luke19:39)

* **Associated Passages:** John 12:3; John 19:39

## λογεία (id: 003068000000000)

λογεία
======

λογεία (G3048)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 λέγω

57\.66 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Take, Obtain, Gain, Lose

collection the act of collecting contributions, especially those involving voluntary response In some instances it may be important to translate λογεία as ‘to receive gifts of money,’ but the focus is upon the activity of the person or persons engaged in obtaining the contributions. This may be expressed in some instances as ‘to go from one person to another to receive their contributions.’

[1CO 16:1](https://ref.ly/Rom16:1) · [1CO 16:2](https://ref.ly/Rom16:2)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 16:1; 1 Corinthians 16:2


## λογίζομαι (id: 003069000000000)

λογίζομαι
=========

λογίζομαι (G3049)

λέγω

30\.9 · Think · To Think, Thought

to think about, to reason about, to ponder, reasoning to think about something in a detailed and logical manner

[JHN 11:50](https://ref.ly/Luke11:50) · [1CO 13:11](https://ref.ly/Rom13:11) · [2CO 10:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:7) · [2CO 10:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:11) · [PHP 4:8](https://ref.ly/Eph4:8)

29\.4 · Memory and Recall · Storing of Information

to keep a record, to remember, to bear in mind to keep a mental record of events for the sake of some future action ‘To keep a mental record of something’ may be rendered as ‘to add up in one’s mind’ or ‘to make a list in one’s heart.’

[1CO 13:5](https://ref.ly/Rom13:5) · [2CO 5:19](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:19) · [2TI 4:16](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:16)

31\.1 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Have an Opinion, Hold a View

to hold a view, to have an opinion, to consider, to regard to hold a view or have an opinion with regard to something

[LUK 22:37](https://ref.ly/Mark22:37) · [ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27) · [ROM 2:3](https://ref.ly/Acts2:3) · [ROM 3:28](https://ref.ly/Acts3:28) · [ROM 6:11](https://ref.ly/Acts6:11) · [ROM 8:18](https://ref.ly/Acts8:18) · [ROM 8:36](https://ref.ly/Acts8:36) · [ROM 9:8](https://ref.ly/Acts9:8) · [ROM 14:14](https://ref.ly/Acts14:14) · [1CO 4:1](https://ref.ly/Rom4:1) · [2CO 3:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:5) · [2CO 10:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:2) · [2CO 10:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:2) · [2CO 11:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:5) · [2CO 12:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:6) · [PHP 3:13](https://ref.ly/Eph3:13) · [HEB 11:19](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:19) · [1PE 5:12](https://ref.ly/Jas5:12)

57\.227 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Keep Records

to put into one’s account, to charge one’s account, to regard as an account to keep records of commercial accounts, involving both debits and credits

[ROM 2:26](https://ref.ly/Acts2:26) · [ROM 4:3](https://ref.ly/Acts4:3) · [ROM 4:4](https://ref.ly/Acts4:4) · [ROM 4:5](https://ref.ly/Acts4:5) · [ROM 4:6](https://ref.ly/Acts4:6) · [ROM 4:8](https://ref.ly/Acts4:8) · [ROM 4:9](https://ref.ly/Acts4:9) · [ROM 4:10](https://ref.ly/Acts4:10) · [ROM 4:11](https://ref.ly/Acts4:11) · [ROM 4:22](https://ref.ly/Acts4:22) · [ROM 4:23](https://ref.ly/Acts4:23) · [ROM 4:24](https://ref.ly/Acts4:24) · [GAL 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:6) · [JAS 2:23](https://ref.ly/Heb2:23)

## λογικός (id: 003070000000000)

λογικός
=======

λογικός (G3050)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 λέγω

73\.5 · Genuine, Phony

rational, genuine, true pertaining to being genuine, in the sense of being true to the real and essential nature of something Since in [1PE 2:2](https://ref.ly/Jas2:2) the context is figurative, some translators have preferred to render λογικός as ‘spiritual,’ so as to make the reference not literal but figurative.

[ROM 12:1](https://ref.ly/Acts12:1) · [1PE 2:2](https://ref.ly/Jas2:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 12:1; 1 Peter 2:2

## λόγιος (id: 003072000000000)

λόγιος
======

λόγιος (G3052)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-α, \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 λέγω

33\.32 · Communication · Language Levels

eloquent pertaining to attractive and convincing speech It is also possible to understand λόγιος in [ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24) as meaning ‘learned’ (see [27\.20](#27.20)).

[ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24)

27\.20 · Learn · Learn

learned, cultured pertaining to one who has learned a great deal of the intellectual heritage of a culture It is also possible to understand λόγιος in [ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24) as meaning ‘eloquent’ (see [33\.32](#33.32)).

[ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24)

## λογισμός (id: 003073000000000)

λογισμός
========

λογισμός (G3053)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ 

|  |
| --- |

 λέγω

30\.9 · Think · To Think, Thought

to think about, to reason about, to ponder, reasoning to think about something in a detailed and logical manner

[ROM 2:15](https://ref.ly/Acts2:15)

30\.11 · Think · To Think, Thought

false reasoning, false arguments fallacious and deceptive reasoning and, by implication, based on evil intentions It may be difficult in some languages to speak of ‘false arguments,’ especially if the equivalent of ‘arguments’ is a verb meaning ‘to argue’ or ‘to discuss against someone.‘ One can, however, express the semantic content of ‘false arguments’ (as reflected in λογισμός\[b]) by translating as ‘what people say when they argue, but their words are not true’ or ‘they argue with words that are not true.’

[2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 2:15; 2 Corinthians 10:4

## λόγος (id: 003076000000000)

λόγος
=====

λόγος (G3056)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 λέγω

33\.98 · Communication · Speak, Talk

word, saying, message, statement, question that which has been stated or said, with primary focus upon the content of the communication Any difference of meaning between λόγος\[a] and ῥῆμα\[b] would be only a matter of stylistic usage.  
In [MAT 21:24](https://ref.ly/Matt21:24) λόγος may be rendered as ‘question’ in view of the preceding ἐρωτάω\[a] ‘to ask’ ([33\.180](#33.180)).

57\.228 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Keep Records

account, credit, debit a record of assets and liabilities The phrase εἰς λόγον in [PHP 4:17](https://ref.ly/Eph4:17) is a technical expression referring to the settlement of an account and indicates that this is a credit to the account. Accordingly, one may properly translate λόγον as ‘the amount of an account.’

31\.2 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Have an Opinion, Hold a View

**Collocation:** λόγου ποιέομαι

to consider, to regard, to hold a view, to be of the opinion (an idiom, literally: to make of reason) to have an opinion based on some reason

[ACT 20:24](https://ref.ly/John20:24)3

1 λόγος\[c], particularly in contexts such as [COL 3:16](https://ref.ly/Phil3:16) and [ACT 19:20](https://ref.ly/John19:20), represents a highly specialized meaning of λόγος in the NT. Compare [MRK 2:2](https://ref.ly/Matt2:2), ἐλάλει αὐτοῖς τὸν λόγον ‘he talked to them about the gospel,’ and [LUK 1:2](https://ref.ly/Mark1:2), ὑπηρέται γενόμενοι τοῦ λόγου ‘being servants of the good news.’ 2 λόγος\[d] appears to differ from γράμμα\[b] ([33\.50](#33.50)) in denoting a somewhat more formal treatment of the subject matter. 3 ACT 20:24 In [ACT 20:24](https://ref.ly/John20:24) the negation οὐδενός has been syntactically combined with λόγου rather than with τιμίαν, with which it is semantically more closely connected. Compare English ‘I didn’t think he would go’ in contrast with ‘I thought he would not go.’

## λουτρόν (id: 003085000000000)

λουτρόν
=======

λουτρόν (G3067)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ 

|  |
| --- |

 λουτρόν

53\.43 · Religious Activities · Baptize

washing, baptism ceremonial washing referring to baptism In [EPH 5:26](https://ref.ly/Gal5:26) the phrase τῷ λουτρῷ τοῦ ὕδατος has been generally interpreted as a reference to baptism, since the literal washing of an object by means of water would not be a means of ritual purification in the sense in which the church would be dedicated or consecrated to God. Similarly, in [TIT 3:5](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:5), λουτρόν has generally been regarded as referring to baptism.

[EPH 5:26](https://ref.ly/Gal5:26) · [TIT 3:5](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 5:26; Titus 3:5

## λύκος (id: 003092000000000)

λύκος
=====

λύκος (G3074)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

4\.11 · Animals · Animals

wolf wild, four\-footed, predatory canine; light\-brown fur, similar to jackal, but much bigger; Canis lupus; regarded as ravenous and fierce; commonly prey on flocks; symbol of roaming, opportunistic, dangerous, fierce, and clever banditry In areas of the world in which wolves are not known, some translators have rendered λύκος\[a] by the local equivalent of ‘leopard’ or ‘jaguar.’ This may be satisfactory for initial translations of the Scriptures, but such shifts in reference are normally rejected at a later stage by those readers who become more acquainted with the types animals which exist in other parts of the world. In most instances in which local terms for ‘wolf’ do not exist, translators have used descriptive phrases such as ‘wild dog’ or ‘fierce, wild dog,’ or they may have borrowed a term from a dominant language in the area and have added a qualifying phrase, for example, ‘a wild animal called wolf.’ One may, of course, simply use a more generic expression with some kind of qualifier. For example, in [ACT 20:29](https://ref.ly/John20:29) it is possible to use ‘fierce, wild animals,’ for the meaning of the passage is primarily figurative, and a specific designation of wolf is not required.

[MAT 10:16](https://ref.ly/Matt10:16) · [LUK 10:3](https://ref.ly/Mark10:3) · [JHN 10:12](https://ref.ly/Luke10:12) · [JHN 10:12](https://ref.ly/Luke10:12)

88\.121 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Bad, Evil, Harmful, Damaging

vicious person, fierce wolf, fierce person (a figurative extension of meaning of λύκος\[a] ‘wolf,’ [4\.11](#4.11)) a person who is particularly vicious and dangerous In situations where wolves are not known, it may be possible to translate [ACT 20:29](https://ref.ly/John20:29) as ‘men like fierce animals will come among you.’ In some instances λύκος in [ACT 20:29](https://ref.ly/John20:29) has been rendered as ‘fierce, wild dogs.’

[MAT 7:15](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15) · [ACT 20:29](https://ref.ly/John20:29)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:16; Luke 10:3; John 10:12; Matthew 7:15; Acts 20:29


## λυμαίνω (id: 003093000000000)

λυμαίνω
=======

λυμαίνω (G3075) — λυμαίνομαι

20\.24 · (λυμαίνομαι\[a]) · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

to injure severely, to maltreat to cause injury or harm by maltreatment It is also possible that λυμαίνομαι in [ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3) may mean ‘to destroy’ (see [20\.31](#20.31)).

[ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3)

20\.31 · (λυμαίνομαι\[b]) · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

to ruin, to destroy, destruction to destroy or to cause the destruction of persons, objects, or institutions In a number of languages it is difficult to find a general term for ‘destruction.’ What has often happened is the extension of meaning from a more specific type of reference, for example, ‘to smash,’ to a more generic meaning of ‘to destroy,’ and whether one understands the specific or more generic meaning depends largely upon the context. Accordingly, in [ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3) one may find a figurative usage of a term meaning ‘to smash’ (though understood in a more generic sense), for example, ‘Saul then worked in order to smash the church.’  
It is also possible that λυμαίνομαι in [ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3) may mean ‘to injure severely’ (see [20\.24](#20.24)).

[ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 8:3

## λύσις (id: 003098000000000)

λύσις
=====

λύσις (G3080)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-εως 

|  |
| --- |

 λύω

34\.78 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

to divorce, to separate to dissolve the marriage bond Expressions for divorce are often based on terms meaning literally ‘to send away,’ ‘to separate from,’ or ‘to leave one another.’ However, in a number of languages idiomatic expressions are employed, for example ‘to send him off with his clothes,’ ‘to untie the knot between them,’ or ‘to throw away her hearthstones.’  
Some persons have attempted to make an important distinction between ἀφίημι in [1CO 7:11](https://ref.ly/Rom7:11) and χωρίζω in [1CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/Rom7:15) on the assumption that ἀφίημι implies legal divorce, while χωρίζω only relates to separation. Such a distinction, however, seems to be quite artificial.

[1CO 7:27](https://ref.ly/Rom7:27)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 7:27


## λυσιτελέω (id: 003099000000000)

λυσιτελέω
=========

λύω \+ τελέω

65\.44 · (λυσιτελεῖ) · Value · Advantageous, Not Advantageous

to be advantageous, to be better off, to be to someone’s advantage to be of an advantage to someone In a number of languages the idea of ‘advantage’ implies some comparison, either a benefit which is greater than someone else has or a benefit which makes one’s later state better off than the previous state. For example, in the case of [JHN 11:50](https://ref.ly/Luke11:50) one may translate ‘don’t you realize that if one man dies for the people, then you are much better off.’

[LUK 17:2](https://ref.ly/Mark17:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 17:2

## λυτρόω (id: 003102000000000)

λυτρόω
======

λυτρόω (G3084) — λυτρόομαι

λύω

37\.128 · (λυτρόομαι) · Control, Rule · Release, Set Free

to set free, to liberate, to deliver, liberation, deliverance to release or set free, with the implied analogy to the process of freeing a slave1 In a number of languages one cannot speak of ‘being set free’ without specifying the particular manner or circumstances involved. In the case of [LUK 24:21](https://ref.ly/Mark24:21), for example, it may be necessary to translate ‘to liberate Israel’ as ‘to cause Israel to be free from foreign control’ or ‘... from the power of Rome.’ A similar type of translation may be required in [LUK 2:38](https://ref.ly/Mark2:38), but in the case of [EPH 1:7](https://ref.ly/Gal1:7) it may be necessary to specify ‘we are set free from sin’ or ‘we are set free from our bad desires.’

[LUK 24:21](https://ref.ly/Mark24:21) · [TIT 2:14](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:14) · [1PE 1:18](https://ref.ly/Jas1:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 24:21; Titus 2:14; 1 Peter 1:18

## λύω (id: 003107000000000)

λύω
===

λύω (G3089)

ἀκατάλυτος · ἀλυσιτελής · ἀνάλυσις · ἀναλύω · ἀντίλυτρον · ἀπολύτρωσις · ἀπολύω · διαλύω · ἐκλύομαι · ἐπίλυσις · ἐπιλύω · κατάλυμα · καταλύω · λύσις · λυσιτελεῖ · λύτρον · λυτρόομαι · λύτρωσις · λυτρωτής · παραλύομαι · παραλυτικός

18\.18 · Attachment · Fasten, Stick To

to untie, to loosen to reverse the result of tying by untying

[MAT 16:19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:19) · [MAT 21:2](https://ref.ly/Matt21:2) · [MRK 1:7](https://ref.ly/Matt1:7) · [MRK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Matt7:35) · [MRK 11:2](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2) · [MRK 11:4](https://ref.ly/Matt11:4) · [MRK 11:5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5) · [LUK 3:16](https://ref.ly/Mark3:16) · [LUK 13:15](https://ref.ly/Mark13:15) · [LUK 19:30](https://ref.ly/Mark19:30) · [LUK 19:31](https://ref.ly/Mark19:31) · [LUK 19:33](https://ref.ly/Mark19:33) · [LUK 19:33](https://ref.ly/Mark19:33) · [JHN 1:27](https://ref.ly/Luke1:27) · [JHN 11:44](https://ref.ly/Luke11:44) · [ACT 2:24](https://ref.ly/John2:24) · [ACT 7:33](https://ref.ly/John7:33) · [ACT 13:25](https://ref.ly/John13:25) · [ACT 22:30](https://ref.ly/John22:30)

37\.127 · Control, Rule · Release, Set Free

to release, to set free to release from control, to set free (highly generic meaning applicable to a wide variety of circumstances, including confinement, political domination, sin, sickness)1 In a number of languages there are problems with a somewhat literal translation of λυθῆναι ἀπὸ τοῦ δεσμοῦ τούτου in [LUK 13:16](https://ref.ly/Mark13:16) since the expression is highly figurative. The reference, of course, is to the woman’s condition as a cripple. Furthermore, it may not make sense to speak of ‘Satan binding’ such a person, as in the first part of verse 16\. In a number of languages, therefore, one may speak of ‘Satan causing the woman to be a cripple,’ and then in the latter part of verse 16, one may speak of ‘causing a person no longer to be a cripple.’

[LUK 13:16](https://ref.ly/Mark13:16) · [1CO 7:27](https://ref.ly/Rom7:27) · [REV 1:5](https://ref.ly/Jude1:5) · [REV 9:14](https://ref.ly/Jude9:14) · [REV 9:15](https://ref.ly/Jude9:15) · [REV 20:3](https://ref.ly/Jude20:3) · [REV 20:7](https://ref.ly/Jude20:7)

20\.53 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

to destroy, to tear down, to break to pieces to destroy or reduce something to ruin by tearing down or breaking to pieces In some languages there may be an important distinction in terms meaning ‘to destroy,’ depending upon whether the destruction is purposeful or not. A still further distinction may arise on the basis of beneficial or non\-beneficial results. In [EPH 2:14](https://ref.ly/Gal2:14) the destruction is regarded as beneficial, while in [ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41) the opposite is the case.

[JHN 2:19](https://ref.ly/Luke2:19) · [ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41) · [EPH 2:14](https://ref.ly/Gal2:14) · [2PE 3:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:10) · [2PE 3:11](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:11) · [2PE 3:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:12)

15\.139 · Linear Movement · Disperse, Scatter

to dismiss, to disperse to cause a gathering to be dismissed or dispersed In some languages it may be more appropriate to render this expression in [ACT 13:43](https://ref.ly/John13:43) as ‘when most of the people had left’ or ‘when the meeting was over.’

[ACT 13:43](https://ref.ly/John13:43)

36\.30 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Obey, Disobey

to break (a law), to transgress the failure to conform to a law or regulation, with a possible implication of regarding it as invalid See also discussion at [36\.29](#36.29).

[MAT 5:19](https://ref.ly/Matt5:19) · [JHN 5:18](https://ref.ly/Luke5:18) · [JHN 7:23](https://ref.ly/Luke7:23)

37\.47 · Control, Rule · Exercise Authority

to permit, to allow to exercise authority over something on the basis of its being legitimate There are a number of different interpretations of the implication of this statement in [MAT 16:19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:19), and translators should carefully review this passage in various commentaries.

[MAT 16:19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:19) · [MAT 18:18](https://ref.ly/Matt18:18) · [MAT 18:18](https://ref.ly/Matt18:18)

13\.38 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to do away with, to remove, to eliminate to cause a state to cease2

[ACT 2:24](https://ref.ly/John2:24) · [REV 5:2](https://ref.ly/Jude5:2)

13\.100 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Exist

to cause to come to an end, to cause to become nothing, to put an end to to cause to cease to exist

[JHN 10:35](https://ref.ly/Luke10:35) · [1JN 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:8)3

1 It is possible that ἀπολύω\[c] is somewhat more emphatic in meaning than λύω\[b] in view of the prepositional prefix ἀπο, but NT contexts are not sufficient to indicate any precise degree of distinction. The same possible distinction also applies to the meanings in [37\.128](#37.128). 2 There are undoubtedly some significant differences of meaning in this series in [13\.38](#13.38), but it is not possible to determine the distinctive differences on the basis of existing contexts. 3 1JN 3:8 The phrase τὰ ἔργα τοῦ διαβόλου ‘the works of the Devil’ may be regarded either as something which the Devil has done and therefore something which exists (in which case the meaning of λύω is appropriately in Domain 13\), or the phrase could mean ‘what the Devil is doing,’ and accordingly λύω could be interpreted as a type of aspect, that is to say, it would mean ‘causing an activity to cease.’ There are a number of such problems involved in meanings which may be interpreted as fitting either into Domain 13 or into Domain 68 Aspect.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 16:19; Matthew 21:2; Mark 1:7; Mark 7:35; Mark 11:2; Mark 11:4; Mark 11:5; Luke 3:16; Luke 13:15; Luke 19:30; Luke 19:31; Luke 19:33; John 1:27; John 11:44; Acts 2:24; Acts 7:33; Acts 13:25; Acts 22:30; Luke 13:16; 1 Corinthians 7:27; Revelation 1:5; Revelation 9:14; Revelation 9:15; Revelation 20:3; Revelation 20:7; John 2:19; Acts 27:41; Ephesians 2:14; 2 Peter 3:10; 2 Peter 3:11; 2 Peter 3:12; Acts 13:43; Matthew 5:19; John 5:18; John 7:23; Matthew 18:18; Revelation 5:2; John 10:35; 1 John 3:8
